I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Rails layout not applied when using `render :component`
When upgrading from Rails 7.2 to 8, we encountered an issue where controller layouts are no longer applied when using render :component with server-side rendering in react-rails. [This document](https://github.com/reactjs/react-rails/blob/master/docs/controller-actions.md) talks about this use case, specifically "By default, your current layout will be used and the component, rather than a view, will be rendered in place of yield."

In Rails 7.2.2.1 with react-rails 2.6.2, everything works as expected. The problem is introduced in Rails 8 due to a change in the render pipeline: the point at which layouts are applied has shifted. Specifically, the component renderer adds an `inline` key to the render options. In Rails 7.2, the layout was added before this step, so the presence of the inline key didn't affect the layout being applied. In Rails 8, the pipeline was altered so that the component renderer adds the inline key before the layout is applied, which prevents the layout from being included by default.

[This](https://github.com/rails/rails/commit/42d75ed3a8b96ee4610601ecde7c40e9d65e003f) is the Rails commit that introduced the change. 



</pr_description>

Can you help me implement the necessary changes to the repository so that the requirements specified in the <pr_description> are met?

     5	    # A renderer class suitable for `ActionController::Renderers`.
     6	    # It is associated to `:component` in the Railtie.
     7	    #
     8	    # It is prerendered by default with {React::ServerRendering}.
     9	    # Set options[:prerender] to `false` to disable prerendering.
    10	    #
    11	    # @example Rendering a component from a controller
    12	    #   class TodosController < ApplicationController
    13	    #     def index
    14	    #       @todos = Todo.all
    15	    #       render component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: @todos }, tag: 'span', class: 'todo'
    16	    #     end
    17	    #   end
    18	    class ControllerRenderer
    19	      include React::Rails::ViewHelper
    20	      include ActionView::Helpers::TagHelper
    21	      include ActionView::Helpers::TextHelper
    22	
    23	      attr_accessor :output_buffer
    24	
    25	      def initialize(options = {})
    26	        controller = options[:controller]
    27	        @__react_component_helper = controller.__react_component_helper
    28	      end
    29	
    30	      # @return [String] HTML for `component_name` with `options[:props]`
    31	      def call(component_name, options, &block)
    32	        props = options.fetch(:props, {})
    33	        options = default_options.merge(options.slice(:data, :aria, :tag, :class, :id, :prerender, :camelize_props))
    34	        react_component(component_name, props, options, &block)
    35	      end
    36	
    37	      private
    38	
    39	      def default_options
    40	        { prerender: true }
    41	      end
    42	    end
    43	  end

2026-05-30 17:07:58,324 - INFO - swea-agent-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the issue. Let me look at the PR description more carefully.

The PR description says:
- In Rails 7.2, the layout was added before the component renderer adds an `inline` key
- In Rails 8, the pipeline was altered so that the component renderer adds the `inline` key before the layout is applied, which prevents the layout from being included by default

Looking at the code in `railtie.rb` lines 65-72:

```ruby
initializer "react_rails.add_component_renderer", group: :all do |_app|
  ActionController::Renderers.add :component do |component_name, options|
    renderer = ::React::Rails::ControllerRenderer.new(controller: self)
    html = renderer.call(component_name, options)
    render_options = options.merge(inline: html)
    render(render_options)
  end
end
```

The issue is that when `render :component` is called, it generates HTML and then calls `render` again with `inline: html`. In Rails 8, the `inline` key causes the layout to be skipped because Rails treats `inline` as a special render option that doesn't use layouts.

Let me look at the Rails commit referenced to understand the change: https://github.com/rails/rails/commit/42d75ed3a8b96ee4610601ecde7c40e9d65e003f

Let me search for related test files and understand the expected behavior better

    61	      end
    62	    end

     1	# frozen_string_literal: true
     2	
     3	require "test_helper"
     4	require "fileutils"
     5	
     6	class ServerRenderedHtmlTest < ActionDispatch::IntegrationTest
     7	  SprocketsHelpers.when_available do
     8	    # Rails' asset pipeline has trouble picking up changes to files if they happen too fast.
     9	    # By sleeping for a little bit at certain points, we can make sure that rails notices the
    10	    # change in the file mtime, and calls our renderer setup functions appropriately
    11	    def wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    12	      sleep(1)
    13	    end
    14	
    15	    setup do
    16	      ShakapackerHelpers.compile if ShakapackerHelpers.available?
    17	    end
    18	
    19	    test "react server rendering reloads jsx after changes to the jsx files" do
    20	      if ShakapackerHelpers.available?
    21	        file_with_updates = File.expand_path("helper_files/TodoListWithUpdates.js", __dir__)
    22	        file_without_updates = File.expand_path("helper_files/TodoListWithoutUpdates.js", __dir__)
    23	        app_file = File.expand_path("dummy/app/javascript/components/TodoList.js", __dir__)
    24	      else
    25	        file_with_updates = File.expand_path("helper_files/TodoListWithUpdates.js.jsx", __dir__)
    26	        file_without_updates = File.expand_path("helper_files/TodoListWithoutUpdates.js.jsx", __dir__)
    27	        app_file = File.expand_path("dummy/app/assets/javascripts/components/TodoList.js.jsx", __dir__)
    28	      end
    29	
    30	      FileUtils.cp app_file, file_without_updates
    31	      FileUtils.touch app_file
    32	      wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    33	
    34	      begin
    35	        get "/server/1"
    36	
    37	        refute_match(/Updated/, response.body)
    38	
    39	        FileUtils.cp file_with_updates, app_file
    40	        FileUtils.touch app_file
    41	        if ShakapackerHelpers.available?
    42	          ShakapackerHelpers.compile
    43	        else
    44	          wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    45	        end
    46	
    47	        get "/server/1"
    48	
    49	        assert_match(/Updated/, response.body)
    50	      ensure
    51	        # if we have a test failure, we want to make sure that we revert the dummy file
    52	        FileUtils.mv file_without_updates, app_file
    53	        FileUtils.touch app_file
    54	        wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    55	      end
    56	    end
    57	
    58	    test "it reloads when new jsx files are added to the asset pipeline" do
    59	      assert_raises(ActionView::Template::Error) do
    60	        get "/server/1?component_name=NewList"
    61	      end
    62	
    63	      if ShakapackerHelpers.available?
    64	        new_file_path = "../dummy/app/javascript/components/NewList.js"
    65	        new_file_contents = <<~JS
    66	          var React = require("react")
    67	          module.exports = function() { return <span>"New List"</span> }
    68	        JS
    69	      else
    70	        new_file_path = "../dummy/app/assets/javascripts/components/ZZ_NewComponent.js.jsx"
    71	        new_file_contents = <<~JS
    72	          var NewList = function() { return <span>"New List"</span> }
    73	        JS
    74	      end
    75	
    76	      new_file_path = File.expand_path(new_file_path, __FILE__)
    77	      File.write new_file_path, new_file_contents
    78	
    79	      if ShakapackerHelpers.available?
    80	        ShakapackerHelpers.compile
    81	      else
    82	        wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    83	        FileUtils.touch new_file_path
    84	      end
    85	
    86	      get "/server/1?component_name=NewList"
    87	
    88	      assert_match(/New List/, response.body)
    89	    ensure
    90	      FileUtils.rm_rf(new_file_path)
    91	      wait_to_ensure_asset_pipeline_detects_changes
    92	    end
    93	
    94	    test "react server rendering shows console output as html comment" do # rubocop:disable Minitest/MultipleAssertions
    95	      # Make sure console messages are replayed when requested
    96	      React::ServerRendering.renderer_options = { replay_console: true }
    97	      React::ServerRendering.reset_pool
    98	      get "/server/console_example"
    99	
   100	      assert_match(/Console Logged/, response.body)
   101	      assert_match(/console.log.apply\(console, \["got initial state"\]\)/, response.body)
   102	      assert_match(/console.warn.apply\(console, \["mounted component"\]\)/, response.body)
   103	      assert_match(/console.error.apply\(console, \["rendered!","foo"\]\)/, response.body)
   104	
   105	      # Make sure they're not when we don't ask for them
   106	      React::ServerRendering.renderer_options = { replay_console: false }
   107	      React::ServerRendering.reset_pool
   108	
   109	      get "/server/console_example"
   110	
   111	      assert_match(/Console Logged/, response.body)
   112	      assert_no_match(/console.log/, response.body)
   113	      assert_no_match(/console.warn/, response.body)
   114	      assert_no_match(/console.error/, response.body)
   115	    end
   116	
   117	    test "react inline component rendering (pre-rendered)" do # rubocop:disable Minitest/MultipleAssertions
   118	      get "/server/inline_component_prerender_true"
   119	      rendered_html = response.body
   120	
   121	      assert_match(/<span.*data-react-class="TodoList"/, rendered_html)
   122	      # make sure that the items are prerendered
   123	      assert_match(/Render this inline/, rendered_html)
   124	      assert_match(%r{</ul></span>}, rendered_html, "it accepts a tag override")
   125	      # make sure that prerendered items are marked
   126	      assert_match(/data-hydrate="t"/, rendered_html)
   127	      # make sure that the layout is rendered with the component
   128	      assert_match(%r{<title>Dummy</title>}, rendered_html)
   129	      # make sure that custom html attributes are rendered
   130	      assert_match(/class="custom-class"/, rendered_html)
   131	      assert_match(/id="custom-id"/, rendered_html)
   132	      assert_match(/data-remote="true"/, rendered_html)
   133	    end
   134	
   135	    test "react inline component rendering (not pre-rendered)" do
   136	      get "/server/inline_component_prerender_false"
   137	      rendered_html = response.body
   138	      # make sure the tag closes immediately:
   139	      assert_match(%r{<span.*data-react-class="TodoList"[^<]*></span>}, rendered_html)
   140	    end
   141	
   142	    test "react inline component rendering with camelize_props (pre-rendered)" do
   143	      get "/server/inline_component_with_camelize_props_prerender_true"
   144	      rendered_html = response.body
   145	
   146	      assert_match(/data-react-props.*testCamelizeProps.*true/, rendered_html)
   147	    end
   148	
   149	    test "react inline component rendering with camelize_props (not pre-rendered)" do
   150	      get "/server/inline_component_with_camelize_props_prerender_false"
   151	      rendered_html = response.body
   152	
   153	      assert_match(/data-react-props.*testCamelizeProps.*true/, rendered_html)
   154	    end
   155	  end
   156	end

2026-05-30 17:08:29,223 - INFO - swea-agent-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - 💭 THOUGHT
So the current base gemfile uses Rails 7.0.x. The PR description mentions this is an issue that appears in Rails 8. The fix should be in react-rails to ensure layouts work properly even when `inline` is used.

Let me understand the problem better. The issue is in the `add_component_renderer` initializer:

```ruby
ActionController::Renderers.add :component do |component_name, options|
  renderer = ::React::Rails::ControllerRenderer.new(controller: self)
  html = renderer.call(component_name, options)
  render_options = options.merge(inline: html)
  render(render_options)
end
```

When `render :component` is called, the renderer generates HTML and then calls `render` with `inline: html`. In older Rails versions, the layout was applied before the inline rendering was processed. But now in Rails 8, `inline` bypasses the layout.

The fix should be to ensure the layout is applied. We need to pass the layout along with the render options.

Let me check if there's a way to see what options are available. Let me look at the test setup more

🎬 ACTION

    91	    #
    92	    #     render json: { hello: "world" }
    93	    #     # => renders "{\"hello\":\"world\"}"
    94	    #
    95	    # By default, when a rendering mode is specified, no layout template is
    96	    # rendered.
    97	    #
    98	    # ==== Options
    99	    #
   100	    # [+:assigns+]
   101	    #   Hash of instance variable assignments for the template.
   102	    #
   103	    #     render inline: "<h1>Hello, <%= @name %>!</h1>", assigns: { name: "World" }
   104	    #     # => renders "<h1>Hello, World!</h1>"
   105	    #
   106	    # [+:locals+]
   107	    #   Hash of local variable assignments for the template.
   108	    #
   109	    #     render inline: "<h1>Hello, <%= name %>!</h1>", locals: { name: "World" }
   110	    #     # => renders "<h1>Hello, World!</h1>"
   111	    #
   112	    # [+:layout+]
   113	    #   The layout template to render. Can also be +false+ or +true+ to disable
   114	    #   or (re)enable the default layout template.
   115	    #
   116	    #     render "posts/show", layout: "holiday"
   117	    #     # => renders app/views/posts/show.html.erb with the app/views/layouts/holiday.html.erb layout
   118	    #
   119	    #     render "posts/show", layout: false
   120	    #     # => renders app/views/posts/show.html.erb with no layout
   121	    #
   122	    #     render inline: "<h1>Hello, World!</h1>", layout: true
   123	    #     # => renders "<h1>Hello, World!</h1>" with the default layout
   124	    #
   125	    # [+:status+]
   126	    #   The HTTP status code to send with the response. Can be specified as a
   127	    #   number or as the status name in Symbol form. Defaults to 200.
   128	    #
   129	    #     render "posts/new", status: 422
   130	    #     # => renders app/views/posts/new.html.erb with HTTP status code 422
   131	    #
   132	    #     render "posts/new", status: :unprocessable_entity
   133	    #     # => renders app/views/posts/new.html.erb with HTTP status code 422
   134	    #
   135	    #--
   136	    # Check for double render errors and set the content_type after rendering.
   137	    def render(*args)
   138	      raise ::AbstractController::DoubleRenderError if response_body
   139	      super
   140	    end
   141	
   142	    # Similar to #render, but only returns the rendered template as a string,
   143	    # instead of setting +self.response_body+.
   144	    #--
   145	    # Override render_to_string because body can now be set to a Rack body.
   146	    def render_to_string(*)
   147	      result = super
   148	      if result.respond_to?(:each)
   149	        string = +""
   150	        result.each { |r| string << r }
   151	        string
   152	      else
   153	        result
   154	      end
   155	    end
   156	
   157	    def render_to_body(options = {}) # :nodoc:
   158	      super || _render_in_priorities(options) || " "
   159	    end
   160	
   161	    private
   162	      # Before processing, set the request formats in current controller formats.
   163	      def process_action(*) # :nodoc:
   164	        self.formats = request.formats.filter_map(&:ref)
   165	        super
   166	      end
   167	
   168	      def _process_variant(options)
   169	        if defined?(request) && !request.nil? && request.variant.present?
   170	          options[:variant] = request.variant
   171	        end
   172	      end
   173	
   174	      def _render_in_priorities(options)
   175	        RENDER_FORMATS_IN_PRIORITY.each do |format|
   176	          return options[format] if options.key?(format)
   177	        end
   178	
   179	        nil
   180	      end
   181	
   182	      def _set_html_content_type
   183	        self.content_type = Mime[:html].to_s
   184	      end
   185	
   186	      def _set_rendered_content_type(format)
   187	        if format && !response.media_type
   188	          self.content_type = format.to_s
   189	        end
   190	      end
   191	
   192	      def _set_vary_header
   193	        if response.headers["Vary"].blank? && request.should_apply_vary_header?
   194	          response.headers["Vary"] = "Accept"
   195	        end
   196	      end
   197	
   198	      # Normalize arguments by catching blocks and setting them on :update.
   199	      def _normalize_args(action = nil, options = {}, &blk)
   200	        options = super
   201	        options[:update] = blk if block_given?
   202	        options
   203	      end
   204	
   205	      # Normalize both text and status options.
   206	      def _normalize_options(options)
   207	        _normalize_text(options)
   208	
   209	        if options[:html]
   210	          options[:html] = ERB::Util.html_escape(options[:html])
   211	        end
   212	
   213	        if options[:status]
   214	          options[:status] = Rack::Utils.status_code(options[:status])
   215	        end
   216	
   217	        super
   218	      end
   219	
   220	      def _normalize_text(options)
   221	        RENDER_FORMATS_IN_PRIORITY.each do |format|
   222	          if options.key?(format) && options[format].respond_to?(:to_text)
   223	            options[format] = options[format].to_text
   224	          end
   225	        end
   226	      end
   227	
   228	      # Process controller specific options, as status, content-type and location.
   229	      def _process_options(options)
   230	        status, content_type, location = options.values_at(:status, :content_type, :location)
   231	
   232	        self.status = status if status
   233	        self.content_type = content_type if content_type
   234	        headers["Location"] = url_for(location) if location
   235	
   236	        super
   237	      end
   238	  end
   239	end

   102	      _process_options(options)
   103	      _render_template(options)

   107	      # Find and render a template based on the options given.
   108	      def _render_template(options)
   109	        variant = options.delete(:variant)
   110	        assigns = options.delete(:assigns)
   111	        context = view_context
   112	
   113	        context.assign assigns if assigns
   114	        lookup_context.variants = variant if variant
   115	
   116	        rendered_template = context.in_rendering_context(options) do |renderer|
   117	          renderer.render_to_object(context, options)
   118	        end
   119	
   120	        rendered_format = rendered_template.format || lookup_context.formats.first
   121	        @rendered_format = Template::Types[rendered_format]
   122	
   123	        rendered_template.body
   124	      end

   127	      def _process_format(format)
   128	        super
   129	        lookup_context.formats = [format.to_sym] if format.to_sym
   130	      end

   132	      # Normalize args by converting render "foo" to render :action => "foo" and
   133	      # render "foo/bar" to render :template => "foo/bar".
   134	      def _normalize_args(action = nil, options = {})
   135	        options = super(action, options)
   136	        case action
   137	        when NilClass
   138	        when Hash
   139	          options = action
   140	        when String, Symbol
   141	          action = action.to_s
   142	          key = action.include?(?/) ? :template : :action
   143	          options[key] = action
   144	        else
   145	          if action.respond_to?(:permitted?) && action.permitted?
   146	            options = action
   147	          elsif action.respond_to?(:render_in)
   148	            options[:renderable] = action
   149	          else
   150	            options[:partial] = action
   151	          end
   152	        end
   153	
   154	        options
   155	      end

   160	        if options[:partial] == true
   161	          options[:partial] = action_name
   162	        end
   163	
   164	        if (options.keys & [:partial, :file, :template]).empty?
   165	          options[:prefixes] ||= _prefixes
   166	        end
   167	
   168	        options[:template] ||= (options[:action] || action_name).to_s
   169	        options
   170	      end
   171	  end

Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /var/lib/gems/3.1.0/gems/actionview-7.0.8.1/lib/action_view/layouts.rb:
     1	# frozen_string_literal: true
     2	
     3	require "action_view/rendering"
     4	require "active_support/core_ext/module/redefine_method"
     5	
     6	module ActionView
     7	  # Layouts reverse the common pattern of including shared headers and footers in many templates to isolate changes in
     8	  # repeated setups. The inclusion pattern has pages that look like this:
     9	  #
    10	  #   <%= render "shared/header" %>
    11	  #   Hello World
    12	  #   <%= render "shared/footer" %>
    13	  #
    14	  # This approach is a decent way of keeping common structures isolated from the changing content, but it's verbose
    15	  # and if you ever want to change the structure of these two includes, you'll have to change all the templates.
    16	  #
    17	  # With layouts, you can flip it around and have the common structure know where to insert changing content. This means
    18	  # that the header and footer are only mentioned in one place, like this:
    19	  #
    20	  #   // The header part of this layout
    21	  #   <%= yield %>
    22	  #   // The footer part of this layout
    23	  #
    24	  # And then you have content pages that look like this:
    25	  #
    26	  #    hello world
    27	  #
    28	  # At rendering time, the content page is computed and then inserted in the layout, like this:
    29	  #
    30	  #   // The header part of this layout
    31	  #   hello world
    32	  #   // The footer part of this layout
    33	  #
    34	  # == Accessing shared variables
    35	  #
    36	  # Layouts have access to variables specified in the content pages and vice versa. This allows you to have layouts with
    37	  # references that won't materialize before rendering time:
    38	  #
    39	  #   <h1><%= @page_title %></h1>
    40	  #   <%= yield %>
    41	  #
    42	  # ...and content pages that fulfill these references _at_ rendering time:
    43	  #
    44	  #    <% @page_title = "Welcome" %>
    45	  #    Off-world colonies offers you a chance to start a new life
    46	  #
    47	  # The result after rendering is:
    48	  #
    49	  #   <h1>Welcome</h1>
    50	  #   Off-world colonies offers you a chance to start a new life
    51	  #
    52	  # == Layout assignment
    53	  #
    54	  # You can either specify a layout declaratively (using the #layout class method) or give
    55	  # it the same name as your controller, and place it in <tt>app/views/layouts</tt>.
    56	  # If a subclass does not have a layout specified, it inherits its layout using normal Ruby inheritance.
    57	  #
    58	  # For instance, if you have PostsController and a template named <tt>app/views/layouts/posts.html.erb</tt>,
    59	  # that template will be used for all actions in PostsController and controllers inheriting
    60	  # from PostsController.
    61	  #
    62	  # If you use a module, for instance Weblog::PostsController, you will need a template named
    63	  # <tt>app/views/layouts/weblog/posts.html.erb</tt>.
    64	  #
    65	  # Since all your controllers inherit from ApplicationController, they will use
    66	  # <tt>app/views/layouts/application.html.erb</tt> if no other layout is specified
    67	  # or provided.
    68	  #
    69	  # == Inheritance Examples
    70	  #
    71	  #   class BankController < ActionController::Base
    72	  #     # bank.html.erb exists
    73	  #
    74	  #   class ExchangeController < BankController
    75	  #     # exchange.html.erb exists
    76	  #
    77	  #   class CurrencyController < BankController
    78	  #
    79	  #   class InformationController < BankController
    80	  #     layout "information"
    81	  #
    82	  #   class TellerController < InformationController
    83	  #     # teller.html.erb exists
    84	  #
    85	  #   class EmployeeController < InformationController
    86	  #     # employee.html.erb exists
    87	  #     layout nil
    88	  #
    89	  #   class VaultController < BankController
    90	  #     layout :access_level_layout
    91	  #
    92	  #   class TillController < BankController
    93	  #     layout false
    94	  #
    95	  # In these examples, we have three implicit lookup scenarios:
    96	  # * The +BankController+ uses the "bank" layout.
    97	  # * The +ExchangeController+ uses the "exchange" layout.
    98	  # * The +CurrencyController+ inherits the layout from BankController.
    99	  #
   100	  # However, when a layout is explicitly set, the explicitly set layout wins:
   101	  # * The +InformationController+ uses the "information" layout, explicitly set.
   102	  # * The +TellerController+ also uses the "information" layout, because the parent explicitly set it.
   103	  # * The +EmployeeController+ uses the "employee" layout, because it set the layout to +nil+, resetting the parent configuration.
   104	  # * The +VaultController+ chooses a layout dynamically by calling the <tt>access_level_layout</tt> method.
   105	  # * The +TillController+ does not use a layout at all.
   106	  #
   107	  # == Types of layouts
   108	  #
   109	  # Layouts are basically just regular templates, but the name of this template needs not be specified statically. Sometimes
   110	  # you want to alternate layouts depending on runtime information, such as whether someone is logged in or not. This can
   111	  # be done either by specifying a method reference as a symbol or using an inline method (as a proc).
   112	  #
   113	  # The method reference is the preferred approach to variable layouts and is used like this:
   114	  #
   115	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   116	  #     layout :writers_and_readers
   117	  #
   118	  #     def index
   119	  #       # fetching posts
   120	  #     end
   121	  #
   122	  #     private
   123	  #       def writers_and_readers
   124	  #         logged_in? ? "writer_layout" : "reader_layout"
   125	  #       end
   126	  #   end
   127	  #
   128	  # Now when a new request for the index action is processed, the layout will vary depending on whether the person accessing
   129	  # is logged in or not.
   130	  #
   131	  # If you want to use an inline method, such as a proc, do something like this:
   132	  #
   133	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   134	  #     layout proc { |controller| controller.logged_in? ? "writer_layout" : "reader_layout" }
   135	  #   end
   136	  #
   137	  # If an argument isn't given to the proc, it's evaluated in the context of
   138	  # the current controller anyway.
   139	  #
   140	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   141	  #     layout proc { logged_in? ? "writer_layout" : "reader_layout" }
   142	  #   end
   143	  #
   144	  # Of course, the most common way of specifying a layout is still just as a plain template name:
   145	  #
   146	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   147	  #     layout "weblog_standard"
   148	  #   end
   149	  #
   150	  # The template will be looked always in <tt>app/views/layouts/</tt> folder. But you can point
   151	  # <tt>layouts</tt> folder direct also. <tt>layout "layouts/demo"</tt> is the same as <tt>layout "demo"</tt>.
   152	  #
   153	  # Setting the layout to +nil+ forces it to be looked up in the filesystem and fallbacks to the parent behavior if none exists.
   154	  # Setting it to +nil+ is useful to re-enable template lookup overriding a previous configuration set in the parent:
   155	  #
   156	  #     class ApplicationController < ActionController::Base
   157	  #       layout "application"
   158	  #     end
   159	  #
   160	  #     class PostsController < ApplicationController
   161	  #       # Will use "application" layout
   162	  #     end
   163	  #
   164	  #     class CommentsController < ApplicationController
   165	  #       # Will search for "comments" layout and fallback "application" layout
   166	  #       layout nil
   167	  #     end
   168	  #
   169	  # == Conditional layouts
   170	  #
   171	  # If you have a layout that by default is applied to all the actions of a controller, you still have the option of rendering
   172	  # a given action or set of actions without a layout, or restricting a layout to only a single action or a set of actions. The
   173	  # <tt>:only</tt> and <tt>:except</tt> options can be passed to the layout call. For example:
   174	  #
   175	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   176	  #     layout "weblog_standard", except: :rss
   177	  #
   178	  #     # ...
   179	  #
   180	  #   end
   181	  #
   182	  # This will assign "weblog_standard" as the WeblogController's layout for all actions except for the +rss+ action, which will
   183	  # be rendered directly, without wrapping a layout around the rendered view.
   184	  #
   185	  # Both the <tt>:only</tt> and <tt>:except</tt> condition can accept an arbitrary number of method references, so
   186	  # <tt>except: [ :rss, :text_only ]</tt> is valid, as is <tt>except: :rss</tt>.
   187	  #
   188	  # == Using a different layout in the action render call
   189	  #
   190	  # If most of your actions use the same layout, it makes perfect sense to define a controller-wide layout as described above.
   191	  # Sometimes you'll have exceptions where one action wants to use a different layout than the rest of the controller.
   192	  # You can do this by passing a <tt>:layout</tt> option to the <tt>render</tt> call. For example:
   193	  #
   194	  #   class WeblogController < ActionController::Base
   195	  #     layout "weblog_standard"
   196	  #
   197	  #     def help
   198	  #       render action: "help", layout: "help"
   199	  #     end
   200	  #   end
   201	  #
   202	  # This will override the controller-wide "weblog_standard" layout, and will render the help action with the "help" layout instead.
   203	  module Layouts
   204	    extend ActiveSupport::Concern
   205	
   206	    include ActionView::Rendering
   207	
   208	    included do
   209	      class_attribute :_layout, instance_accessor: false
   210	      class_attribute :_layout_conditions, instance_accessor: false, default: {}
   211	
   212	      _write_layout_method
   213	    end
   214	
   215	    delegate :_layout_conditions, to: :class
   216	
   217	    module ClassMethods
   218	      def inherited(klass) # :nodoc:
   219	        super
   220	        klass._write_layout_method
   221	      end
   222	
   223	      # This module is mixed in if layout conditions are provided. This means
   224	      # that if no layout conditions are used, this method is not used
   225	      module LayoutConditions # :nodoc:
   226	        private
   227	          # Determines whether the current action has a layout definition by
   228	          # checking the action name against the :only and :except conditions
   229	          # set by the <tt>layout</tt> method.
   230	          #
   231	          # ==== Returns
   232	          # * <tt>Boolean</tt> - True if the action has a layout definition, false otherwise.
   233	          def _conditional_layout?
   234	            return unless super
   235	
   236	            conditions = _layout_conditions
   237	
   238	            if only = conditions[:only]
   239	              only.include?(action_name)
   240	            elsif except = conditions[:except]
   241	              !except.include?(action_name)
   242	            else
   243	              true
   244	            end
   245	          end
   246	      end
   247	
   248	      # Specify the layout to use for this class.
   249	      #
   250	      # If the specified layout is a:
   251	      # String:: the String is the template name
   252	      # Symbol:: call the method specified by the symbol
   253	      # Proc::   call the passed Proc
   254	      # false::  There is no layout
   255	      # true::   raise an ArgumentError
   256	      # nil::    Force default layout behavior with inheritance
   257	      #
   258	      # Return value of +Proc+ and +Symbol+ arguments should be +String+, +false+, +true+, or +nil+
   259	      # with the same meaning as described above.
   260	      #
   261	      # ==== Parameters
   262	      #
   263	      # * <tt>layout</tt> - The layout to use.
   264	      #
   265	      # ==== Options (conditions)
   266	      #
   267	      # * +:only+   - A list of actions to apply this layout to.
   268	      # * +:except+ - Apply this layout to all actions but this one.
   269	      def layout(layout, conditions = {})
   270	        include LayoutConditions unless conditions.empty?
   271	
   272	        conditions.each { |k, v| conditions[k] = Array(v).map(&:to_s) }
   273	        self._layout_conditions = conditions
   274	
   275	        self._layout = layout
   276	        _write_layout_method
   277	      end
   278	
   279	      # Creates a _layout method to be called by _default_layout .
   280	      #
   281	      # If a layout is not explicitly mentioned then look for a layout with the controller's name.
   282	      # if nothing is found then try same procedure to find super class's layout.
   283	      def _write_layout_method # :nodoc:
   284	        silence_redefinition_of_method(:_layout)
   285	
   286	        prefixes = /\blayouts/.match?(_implied_layout_name) ? [] : ["layouts"]
   287	        default_behavior = "lookup_context.find_all('#{_implied_layout_name}', #{prefixes.inspect}, false, [], { formats: formats }).first || super"
   288	        name_clause = if name
   289	          default_behavior
   290	        else
   291	          <<-RUBY
   292	            super
   293	          RUBY
   294	        end
   295	
   296	        layout_definition = \
   297	          case _layout
   298	          when String
   299	            _layout.inspect
   300	          when Symbol
   301	            <<-RUBY
   302	              #{_layout}.tap do |layout|
   303	                return #{default_behavior} if layout.nil?
   304	                unless layout.is_a?(String) || !layout
   305	                  raise ArgumentError, "Your layout method :#{_layout} returned \#{layout}. It " \
   306	                    "should have returned a String, false, or nil"
   307	                end
   308	              end
   309	            RUBY
   310	          when Proc
   311	            define_method :_layout_from_proc, &_layout
   312	            private :_layout_from_proc
   313	            <<-RUBY
   314	              result = _layout_from_proc(#{_layout.arity == 0 ? '' : 'self'})
   315	              return #{default_behavior} if result.nil?
   316	              result
   317	            RUBY
   318	          when false
   319	            nil
   320	          when true
   321	            raise ArgumentError, "Layouts must be specified as a String, Symbol, Proc, false, or nil"
   322	          when nil
   323	            name_clause
   324	          end
   325	
   326	        class_eval <<-RUBY, __FILE__, __LINE__ + 1
   327	          # frozen_string_literal: true
   328	          def _layout(lookup_context, formats)
   329	            if _conditional_layout?
   330	              #{layout_definition}
   331	            else
   332	              #{name_clause}
   333	            end
   334	          end
   335	          private :_layout
   336	        RUBY
   337	      end
   338	
   339	      private
   340	        # If no layout is supplied, look for a template named the return
   341	        # value of this method.
   342	        #
   343	        # ==== Returns
   344	        # * <tt>String</tt> - A template name
   345	        def _implied_layout_name
   346	          controller_path
   347	        end
   348	    end
   349	
   350	    def _normalize_options(options) # :nodoc:
   351	      super
   352	
   353	      if _include_layout?(options)
   354	        layout = options.delete(:layout) { :default }
   355	        options[:layout] = _layout_for_option(layout)
   356	      end
   357	    end
   358	
   359	    attr_internal_writer :action_has_layout
   360	
   361	    def initialize(*) # :nodoc:
   362	      @_action_has_layout = true
   363	      super
   364	    end
   365	
   366	    # Controls whether an action should be rendered using a layout.
   367	    # If you want to disable any <tt>layout</tt> settings for the
   368	    # current action so that it is rendered without a layout then
   369	    # either override this method in your controller to return false
   370	    # for that action or set the <tt>action_has_layout</tt> attribute
   371	    # to false before rendering.
   372	    def action_has_layout?
   373	      @_action_has_layout
   374	    end
   375	
   376	  private
   377	    def _conditional_layout?
   378	      true
   379	    end
   380	
   381	    # This will be overwritten by _write_layout_method
   382	    def _layout(*); end
   383	
   384	    # Determine the layout for a given name, taking into account the name type.
   385	    #
   386	    # ==== Parameters
   387	    # * <tt>name</tt> - The name of the template
   388	    def _layout_for_option(name)
   389	      case name
   390	      when String     then _normalize_layout(name)
   391	      when Proc       then name
   392	      when true       then Proc.new { |lookup_context, formats| _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, true)  }
   393	      when :default   then Proc.new { |lookup_context, formats| _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, false) }
   394	      when false, nil then nil
   395	      else
   396	        raise ArgumentError,
   397	          "String, Proc, :default, true, or false, expected for `layout'; you passed #{name.inspect}"
   398	      end
   399	    end
   400	
   401	    def _normalize_layout(value)
   402	      value.is_a?(String) && !value.match?(/\blayouts/) ? "layouts/#{value}" : value
   403	    end
   404	
   405	    # Returns the default layout for this controller.
   406	    # Optionally raises an exception if the layout could not be found.
   407	    #
   408	    # ==== Parameters
   409	    # * <tt>formats</tt> - The formats accepted to this layout
   410	    # * <tt>require_layout</tt> - If set to +true+ and layout is not found,
   411	    #   an +ArgumentError+ exception is raised (defaults to +false+)
   412	    #
   413	    # ==== Returns
   414	    # * <tt>template</tt> - The template object for the default layout (or +nil+)
   415	    def _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, require_layout = false)
   416	      begin
   417	        value = _layout(lookup_context, formats) if action_has_layout?
   418	      rescue NameError => e
   419	        raise e, "Could not render layout: #{e.message}"
   420	      end
   421	
   422	      if require_layout && action_has_layout? && !value
   423	        raise ArgumentError,
   424	          "There was no default layout for #{self.class} in #{view_paths.inspect}"
   425	      end
   426	
   427	      _normalize_layout(value)
   428	    end
   429

Now I have found the key piece. In Rails 7.0.8.1, the `_include_layout?` method looks at whether the options contain `:inline`:

```ruby
def _include_layout?(options)
  (options.keys & [:body, :plain, :html, :inline, :partial]).empty? || options.key?(:layout)
end
```

This means that if `:inline` is present in the options, a layout is NOT included UNLESS `:layout` is also explicitly specified.

Now, the Rails commit referenced in the PR description (https://github.com/rails/rails/commit/42d75ed3a8b96ee4610601ecde7c40e9d65e003f) likely changed the order of operations. But the core issue is: when the react-rails component renderer calls `render(render_options)` with `inline: html`, the `inline` key causes the layout to be skipped.

The PR description says:
- In Rails 7.2, the layout was added before this step, so the presence of the inline key didn't affect the layout being applied.
- In Rails 8, the pipeline was altered so that the component renderer adds the inline key before the layout is applied, which prevents the layout from being included by default.

Actually, looking at the `_include_layout?` method in Rails 7.0.8.1, it already excludes `inline` from layouts. But wait - the test at line 128 expects the layout to be present:
```ruby
assert_match(%r{<title>Dummy</title>}, rendered_html)
```

     2	
     3	module SprocketsHelpers
     4	  module_function
     5	
     6	  def available?
     7	    # We can't scan for sprockets in gemfile_lock because it's
     8	    #   a dependency of Rails even if not required.
     9	    # We also can't scan for defined?(Sprockets) because this is used to
    10	    #   require Sprockets in the config/application.rb
    11	    # !!Bundler.locked_gems.specs.find {|gem_spec| gem_spec.name == 'sprockets'}
    12	    ENV.fetch("BUNDLE_GEMFILE", nil).include?("sprockets")
    13	  end
    14	
    15	  # The block depends on sprockets, don't run it if sprockets is missing
    16	  def when_available
    17	    return unless available?
    18	
    19	    yield
    20	  end
    21	
    22	  def clear_sprockets_cache
    23	    # Remove cached files
    24	    Rails.root.join("tmp/cache").tap do |tmp|
    25	      tmp.rmtree if tmp.exist?
    26	      tmp.mkpath
    27	    end
    28	  end
    29	
    30	  def fetch_asset_body(asset_logical_path)
    31	    Rails.application.assets[asset_logical_path].to_s
    32	  end
    33	
    34	  # Sprockets 2 doesn't expire this assets well in
    35	  # this kind of setting,
    36	  # so override `fresh?` to mark it as expired.
    37	  def manually_expire_asset(asset_name)
    38	    asset = Rails.application.assets[asset_name]
    39	    def asset.fresh?(_env)
    40	      false
    41	    end
    42	  end
    43	
    44	  def precompile_assets
    45	    invoke_assets_precompile_task
    46	
    47	    if Rails.application.respond_to?(:assets_manifest)
    48	      # Make a new manifest since assets weren't compiled before
    49	      config = Rails.application.config
    50	      path = File.join(config.paths["public"].first, config.assets.prefix)
    51	      new_manifest = Sprockets::Manifest.new(Rails.application.assets, path)
    52	      Rails.application.assets_manifest = new_manifest
    53	    end
    54	
    55	    assets_directory = File.expand_path("../dummy/public/assets", __dir__)
    56	    raise "Asset precompilation failed" unless Dir.exist?(assets_directory)
    57	  end
    58	
    59	  def clear_precompiled_assets
    60	    assets_directory = File.expand_path("../dummy/public/assets", __dir__)
    61	    FileUtils.rm_r(assets_directory)
    62	    ENV.delete("RAILS_GROUPS")
    63	  end

    66	    private

    68	    def invoke_assets_precompile_task
    69	      # Changing directories is required because:
    70	      # - assets:precompile runs webpacker:compile when availabled
    71	      # - webpacker:compile depends on `./bin/webpack`, so `.` must be the app root
    72	      Dir.chdir("./test/dummy") do
    73	        ENV["RAILS_GROUPS"] = "assets" # required for Rails 3.2
    74	        Rake::Task["assets:precompile"].reenable
    75	
    76	        if Rails::VERSION::MAJOR == 3
    77	          Rake::Task["assets:precompile:all"].reenable

    80	        end
    81

    83	      end

1. The renderer generates HTML
2. It merges `inline: html` into the options
3. It calls `render(render_options)` again

2026-05-30 17:10:46,279 - INFO - swea-agent-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me focus on the actual fix. I understand the issue now:

1. The component renderer generates HTML and passes it via `inline:` option
2. In Rails, `inline` is in the list of options that bypass layouts (see `_include_layout?`)
3. The fix should ensure that when the component renderer calls `render`, the layout is preserved

Looking at the code in `railtie.rb`:

```ruby
initializer "react_rails.add_component_renderer", group: :all do |_app|
  ActionController::Renderers.add :component do |component_name, options|
    renderer = ::React::Rails::ControllerRenderer.new(controller: self)
    html = renderer.call(component_name, options)
    render_options = options.merge(inline: html)
    render(render_options)
  end
end
```

The issue is that `options.merge(inline: html)` creates options with `:inline` which then triggers the layout-skipping behavior in `_include_layout?`.

The fix should be to pass `layout: true` (or preserve the original layout behavior) when calling `render`. But we also need to think about what the user may have specified.

Looking at the `_include_layout?` method:
```ruby
def _include_layout?(options)
  (options.keys & [:body, :plain, :html, :inline, :partial]).empty? || options.key?(:layout)
end
```

So if `:layout` is present in the options, the layout WILL be included even if `:inline` is present. The fix should ensure that the layout option is passed through.

But wait, there's a subtlety: the user might call `render component: 'X', layout: false` to explicitly disable the layout. We need to respect that.

Actually, looking more carefully at the flow: when `render component: ...` is called, the options hash includes things like `:component`, `:props`, `:tag`, etc. The renderer creates the HTML, then merges `inline: html` and calls `render` again. 

If the user specified `layout: false`, that should be preserved. If the user didn't specify a layout, the default layout should be applied.

The problem is: when we merge `inline: html` into the options, the `layout` key is not present (unless explicitly given by the user), so `_include_layout?` returns false because `inline` is in the keys.

The fix: we should ensure that the layout is applied by default. We can do this by setting `layout: true` in the render options when no explicit layout is given by the user. But we also need to be careful not to override an explicit `layout: false`.

Let me look at how the options flow:

1. User calls `render component: 'TodoList', props: {...}`
2. Options = `{component: 'TodoList', props: {...}}`
3. The renderer block extracts `component_name` and `options`
4. It generates HTML
5. It merges `inline: html` into options: `{component: 'TodoList', props: {...}, inline: html}`
6. It calls `render(render_options)`

Now, `render` in step 6 goes through the normal rendering pipeline. The `inline` key triggers `_render_template` which renders the inline string. But `_include_layout?` returns false because `inline` is present and `layout` is not.

The fix: we should add `layout: true` to the render options when no layout is explicitly specified. But we need to check if the user explicitly passed `layout: false` or `layout: 'something'`.

Actually, looking at the PR description more carefully: "In Rails 7.2, the layout was added before this step, so the presence of the inline key didn't affect the layout being applied."

This suggests that in Rails 7.2, the layout was determined earlier in the pipeline, before the `inline` key was even considered. In Rails 8, the order changed so that when the renderer adds `inline`, it's too late—the layout has already been determined to be skipped.

But wait, looking at Rails 7.0.8.1's `_include_layout?` method, it already excludes `inline`. So the layout should already be skipped in Rails 7.0.8.1. Let me verify by actually running the test with a proper BUNDLE_GEMFILE

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && BUNDLE_GEMFILE=gemfiles/sprockets_4.gemfile bundle exec ruby -Ilib:test test/server_rendered_html_test.rb -n "test_react_inline_component_rendering_pre-rendered" 2>&1

2026-05-30 17:13:21,511 - DEBUG - swea-lm-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - Response: ModelResponse(id='c15327cd1ba64c33bb109361df8baa26', created=1780161174, model='DeepSeek-V4-Pro', object='chat.completion', system_fingerprint=None, choices=[Choices(finish_reason='tool_calls', index=0, message=Message(content="All tests pass with Rails 7.0.8.1. So the layout is applied correctly even with `inline` key in Rails 7.0.8.1.\n\nWait, but I saw that `_include_layout?` returns false when `inline` is present. How does the layout still get applied?\n\nLet me re-examine the flow. When `render component: 'TodoList', props: {...}` is called:\n1. ActionController::Renderers picks up the `:component` key and calls the renderer block\n2. The block generates HTML, then calls `render(render_options)` where `render_options` includes `inline: html`\n3. This second `render` call goes through the full pipeline again\n\nBut wait - in step 1, when `render` is called with `component:` key, the `render_to_body` method in `ActionController::Renderers` is invoked. It loops through `_renderers` and finds `:component`. It calls the renderer, which generates HTML and calls `render` again. But the first `render` hasn't finished yet - it's still in `render_to_body`. The second `render` call happens within the first one.\n\nActually, looking at the renderers.rb more carefully:\n\n```ruby\ndef _render_to_body_with_renderer(options)\n  _renderers.each do |name|\n    if options.key?(name)\n      _process_options(options)\n      method_name = Renderers._render_with_renderer_method_name(name)\n      return send(method_name, options.delete(name), options)\n    end\n  end\n  nil\nend\n```\n\nSo the renderer for `:component` is called, and it returns the result of `render(render_options)`. The result becomes the body. Then in `render` (abstract_controller/rendering.rb):\n\n```ruby\ndef render(*args, &block)\n  options = _normalize_render(*args, &block)\n  rendered_body = render_to_body(options)\n  ...\n  self.response_body = rendered_body\nend\n```\n\nThe first `render`'s `render_to_body` returns the result of the `:component` renderer, which is the result of the second `render`. So the second `render`'s output becomes the body.\n\nNow, in the second `render`, the options include `inline: html`. Wait, but I saw that `_include_layout?` returns false when `inline` is present. How does the layout still get applied?

Let me re-examine the flow. When `render component: 'TodoList', props: {...}` is called:
1. ActionController::Renderers picks up the `:component` key and calls the renderer block
2. The block generates HTML, then calls `render(render_options)` where `render_options` includes `inline: html`
3. This second `render` call goes through the full pipeline again

But wait - in step 1, when `render` is called with `component:` key, the `render_to_body` method in `ActionController::Renderers` is invoked. It loops through `_renderers` and finds `:component`. It calls the renderer, which generates HTML and calls `render` again. But the first `render` hasn't finished yet - it's still in `render_to_body`. The second `render` call happens within the first one.

Actually, looking at the renderers.rb more carefully:

```ruby
def _render_to_body_with_renderer(options)
  _renderers.each do |name|
    if options.key?(name)
      _process_options(options)
      method_name = Renderers._render_with_renderer_method_name(name)
      return send(method_name, options.delete(name), options)
    end
  end
  nil
end
```

So the renderer for `:component` is called, and it returns the result of `render(render_options)`. The result becomes the body. Then in `render` (abstract_controller/rendering.rb):

```ruby
def render(*args, &block)
  options = _normalize_render(*args, &block)
  rendered_body = render_to_body(options)
  ...
  self.response_body = rendered_body
end
```

The first `render`'s `render_to_body` returns the result of the `:component` renderer, which is the result of the second `render`. So the second `render`'s output becomes the body.

Now, in the second `render`, the options include `inline: html`. In `_normalize_options` (layouts.rb):

```ruby
def _normalize_options(options)
  super
  if _include_layout?(options)
    layout = options.delete(:layout) { :default }
    options[:layout] = _layout_for_option(layout)
  end
end
```

Since `inline` is present and `layout` is not, `_include_layout?` returns false, so no layout is added. Then the inline template is rendered without a layout.

But the test says the layout IS applied! So something else must be happening...

Let me trace through the code more carefully. Maybe the layout is applied at a different level.

Actually wait - let me look at `ActionView::Rendering#render_to_body`:

```ruby
def render_to_body(options = {})
  _process_options(options)
  _render_template(options)
end
```

And `_render_template`:

```ruby
def _render_template(options)
  variant = options.delete(:variant)
  assigns = options.delete(:assigns)
  context = view_context

  context.assign assigns if assigns
  lookup_context.variants = variant if variant

  rendered_template = context.in_rendering_context(options) do |renderer|
    renderer.render_to_object(context, options)
  end

  rendered_format = rendered_template.format || lookup_context.formats.first
  @rendered_format = Template::Types[rendered_format]

  rendered_template.body
end
```

The layout is applied in the `render_to_object` method, which uses the `:layout` option from the options hash.

Now let me check `ActionController::Metal#render_to_body`:

```ruby
def render_to_body(options = {})
  _render_to_body_with_renderer(options) || super
end
```

This calls `_render_to_body_with_renderer` first, which checks for renderer keys (like `:component`). If found, it calls the renderer and returns its result. If not found, it falls through to `super` (which is `ActionView::Rendering#render_to_body`).

So when the user calls `render component: 'TodoList', props: {...}`, the flow is:
1. `render(component: 'TodoList', props: {...})` called
2. `render_to_body({component: 'TodoList', props: {...}})` called
3. `_render_to_body_with_renderer` finds `:component` key
4. Calls the component renderer with `('TodoList', {props: {...}})`
5. Component renderer generates HTML, then calls `render({props: {...}, inline: html})`
6. This second `render` goes through the same path, but `_render_to_body_with_renderer` doesn't find any renderer key (since `:component` was removed), so falls through to `super` -> `ActionView::Rendering#render_to_body`
7. `_normalize_options` is called, which checks `_include_layout?` - since `inline` is present, no layout is added
8. `_render_template` renders the inline HTML without layout

But this should result in no layout! Yet the tests pass. Let me check if there's something else going on.

Wait, maybe I should check how `_normalize_options` works in the context of the second `render` call. The second `render` is called from within the renderer block, which is executed in the context of the controller instance. So `_normalize_options` from `Layouts` module should be called.

Let me check if perhaps the `_include_layout?` method has been overridden or if there's something else:

The bundler/inline approach has issues. Let me just use the existing test setup to debug this.

Let me think about this differently. The PR description says the issue was introduced by a Rails commit that changed the order of the render pipeline. The fix should be in react-rails to ensure layouts work with `render :component` even when Rails changes the pipeline.

The current code passes `inline: html` which causes `_include_layout?` to return false. The simplest fix would be to explicitly pass `layout: true` when no layout is specified by the user. But we need to check if the user explicitly passed a layout option.

Let me look at the options hash more carefully. When a user calls:
```ruby
render component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: [...] }
```

The options hash is:
```ruby
{ component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: [...] } }
```

The renderer adds `inline: html` to it. But the user could also pass `layout: false` or `layout: 'custom'`:
```ruby
render component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: [...] }, layout: false
```

In this case, the options hash would be:
```ruby
{ component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: [...] }, layout: false }
```

And after merging:
```ruby
{ component: 'TodoList', props: { todos: [...] }, layout: false, inline: html }
```

In this case, `_include_layout?` would return true (because `layout` key is present), and then `_layout_for_option(false)` would return `nil`, which means no layout. That's correct.

For the default case (no explicit layout), we want the layout to be applied. So we should add `layout: true` to the render options when no `layout` key is present.

But wait, there's another issue: what if the user has a controller with `layout false` (no layout at all)? If we force `layout: true`, we'd override that. Let me check how controller-level layout settings work.

The controller-level layout setting is applied in `_normalize_options`:
```ruby
def _normalize_options(options)
  super
  if _include_layout?(options)
    layout = options.delete(:layout) { :default }
    options[:layout] = _layout_for_option(layout)
  end
end
```

If `_include_layout?` returns true and no `:layout` key is in options, it defaults to `:default`, which triggers `_default_layout` lookup. If `_include_layout?` returns false, no layout is set and the template is rendered without one.

So the issue is that `inline` causes `_include_layout?` to return false.

The fix: we need to ensure that when we call `render` with `inline:`, the layout is still applied by default. We can do this by explicitly passing `layout: true` in the render options, but only if the user didn't explicitly set a layout.

Here's my proposed fix for the railtie.rb:

```ruby
initializer "react_rails.add_component_renderer", group: :all do |_app|
  ActionController::Renderers.add :component do |component_name, options|
    renderer = ::React::Rails::ControllerRenderer.new(controller: self)
    html = renderer.call(component_name, options)
    render_options = options.merge(inline: html)
    render_options[:layout] = true unless render_options.key?(:layout)
    render(render_options)
  end
end
```

This way:
- If the user didn't specify `layout`, we set `layout: true` to ensure the default layout is applied
- If the user specified `layout: false` or `layout: 'custom'`, we respect that

But wait, I should also check if there's a possibility that the user wants no layout (e.g., controller-level `layout false`). In that case, the controller's `_normalize_options` would set `layout: false` if the user didn't specify one. But our change would override that.

Actually, let me think about this more. The controller-level `layout false` means `action_has_layout?` returns false. Let me check where that comes into play.

Looking at `_default_layout`:
```ruby
def _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, require_layout = false)
  begin
    value = _layout(lookup_context, formats) if action_has_layout?
  ...
end
```

And `_layout_for_option`:
```ruby
def _layout_for_option(name)
  case name
  when String     then _normalize_layout(name)
  when Proc       then name
  when true       then Proc.new { |lookup_context, formats| _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, true)  }
  when :default   then Proc.new { |lookup_context, formats| _default_layout(lookup_context, formats, false) }
  when false, nil then nil
  else
    raise ArgumentError, ...
  end
end
```

So if we pass `layout: true`, it creates a Proc that calls `_default_layout` with `require_layout: true`. `_default_layout` checks `action_has_layout?` first. If the controller has `layout false`, then `action_has_layout?` returns false, and `_default_layout` returns nil, so no layout is applied.

So passing `layout: true` is safe - it still respects the controller-level `layout false` setting.

But what about controllers that use `layout` with conditions like `except:`? That's handled by `_conditional_layout?` in `_layout` method. If `action_has_layout?` is true, `_layout` is called, which checks conditions.

So the fix should be: add `layout: true` when the user hasn't explicitly specified a layout.

2026-05-30 17:18:21,858 - INFO - swea-agent-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - 💭 THOUGHT
OK, the bundler/inline approach is too problematic due to load order issues. Let me rely on the existing test suite instead.

Let me verify my understanding of the problem by looking at the Rails 7.0 source code vs what might change in Rails 8. The key question is: in Rails 7.0.8.1, does `_include_layout?` actually get called when `render :component` is used?

Let me look at the flow more carefully. The component renderer is called from `_render_to_body_with_renderer`:

```ruby
def _render_to_body_with_renderer(options)
  _renderers.each do |name|
    if options.key?(name)
      _process_options(options)
      method_name = Renderers._render_with_renderer_method_name(name)
      return send(method_name, options.delete(name), options)
    end
  end
  nil
end
```

This returns the result of `send(method_name, ...)`. The component renderer calls `render(render_options)` which returns the response body. So the return value of the component renderer is the final response body.

But wait, after `_render_to_body_with_renderer` returns, the result goes back to `render_to_body`:

```ruby
def render_to_body(options)
  _render_to_body_with_renderer(options) || super
end
```

And then back to `render`:

```ruby
def render(*args, &block)
  options = _normalize_render(*args, &block)
  rendered_body = render_to_body(options)
  ...
  self.response_body = rendered_body
end
```

So the first `render`'s `render_to_body` returns the result of the component renderer, which is the result of the second `render` call (which includes the layout or not).

But here's the key: the first `render`'s `_normalize_options` has already been called with the original options (which contain `:component` but not `:inline`). At that point, `_include_layout?` would return true because `:component` is not in the exclusion list (`[:body, :plain, :html, :inline, :partial]`). So a layout would have been added by the first `_normalize_options`.

But wait, the first `_normalize_options` adds layout to the options, but then `_render_to_body_with_renderer` finds `:component` and calls the renderer. The renderer generates HTML and calls `render` again with new options (which include `inline`). The second `render` has its own `_normalize_options` call, which checks `_include_layout?` again with the new options (including `inline`). This time, `_include_layout?` returns false, so no layout is applied.

But the tests pass! So maybe I'm wrong about the flow. Let me check if the second `render` call actually goes through the full pipeline.

Actually, wait. Let me look at the render method in `ActionController::Rendering`:

```ruby
def render(*args)
  raise ::AbstractController::DoubleRenderError if response_body
  super
end
```

The second `render` call happens within the first `render` (via the component renderer). The first `render` hasn't set `response_body` yet (it's still computing it). So the second `render` doesn't raise a double render error. It calls `super` which is `AbstractController::Rendering#render`:

```ruby
def render(*args, &block)
  options = _normalize_render(*args, &block)
  rendered_body = render_to_body(options)
  ...
  self.response_body = rendered_body
end
```

So the second `render` sets `self.response_body` directly! Then it returns. Then the component renderer returns (the return value of `render` which is the rendered body string). Then `_render_to_body_with_renderer` returns that string. Then the first `render_to_body` returns that string. Then the first `render` tries to set `self.response_body` again:

```ruby
def render(*args)
  raise ::AbstractController::DoubleRenderError if response_body
  super
end
```

But wait, the second `render` already set `response_body`. So the first `render` should raise a DoubleRenderError!

But the tests pass, so that doesn't happen. Let me look at this more carefully.

Actually, the second `render` doesn't go through `ActionController::Rendering#render` because it's called from within the renderer block. The renderer block executes in the context of the controller instance. Let me check: when `render(render_options)` is called inside the component renderer block, does it go through `ActionController::Rendering#render`?

The component renderer block is defined using `define_method` in `Renderers.add`:

```ruby
def self.add(key, &block)
  define_method(_render_with_renderer_method_name(key), &block)
  RENDERERS << key.to_sym
end
```

So the block becomes a method on the controller instance. When it calls `render(render_options)`, it calls the controller's `render` method, which is `ActionController::Rendering#render`. That checks for double render and then calls `super`.

But `response_body` hasn't been set yet at that point (the first `render` hasn't finished). So the second `render` proceeds. It sets `response_body`. Then the first `render` checks for double render... but wait, the first `render` already passed the double render check before calling `render_to_body`. So the second `render` sets `response_body`, and then the first `render` continues after `render_to_body` returns and sets `response_body` again, overwriting it. But the double render check only happens at the beginning of `render`, not after.

OK so the flow works, but the second `render` goes through the full pipeline including `_normalize_options` and `_include_layout?`. And `_include_layout?` should return false because of `inline`. So why does the layout still appear?

Let me check if maybe `_include_layout?` is not reached because of some other path. Let me look at `_render_to_body_with_renderer` again:

```ruby
def _render_to_body_with_renderer(options)
  _renderers.each do |name|
    if options.key?(name)
      _process_options(options)
      method_name = Renderers._render_with_renderer_method_name(name)
      return send(method_name, options.delete(name), options)
    end
  end
  nil
end
```

This is called by `ActionController::Metal#render_to_body`:

```ruby
def render_to_body(options = {})
  _render_to_body_with_renderer(options) || super
end
```

The second `render`'s options are `{..., inline: html}`. Does `inline` match any renderer? No, `inline` is not a renderer. So `_render_to_body_with_renderer` returns nil and falls through to `super` which is `ActionView::Rendering#render_to_body`:

```ruby
def render_to_body(options = {})
  _process_options(options)
  _render_template(options)
end
```

And `_render_template` calls `context.in_rendering_context(options)` which eventually renders the inline template.

But wait, where does `_normalize_options` get called for the second `render`? It's called in `_normalize_render`:

```ruby
def _normalize_render(*args, &block)
  options = _normalize_args(*args, &block)
  _process_variant(options)
  _normalize_options(options)
  options
end
```

And `_normalize_options` is overridden in `Layouts`:

```ruby
def _normalize_options(options)
  super
  if _include_layout?(options)
    layout = options.delete(:layout) { :default }
    options[:layout] = _layout_for_option(layout)
  end
end
```

So `_include_layout?` IS called for the second render. And it should return false because `inline` is in the keys. So the layout should NOT be applied.

But the tests pass! Let me actually verify by running the test with the existing code (before my fix) and checking if the layout assertion passes:

2026-05-30 17:19:10,183 - INFO - swea-agent-reactjs__react-rails-1418 - 💭 THOUGHT
OK, tests pass with the original code in Rails 7.0.8.1. But the PR says the issue appears in Rails 8. The referenced commit changed something about the pipeline order.

Let me think about this differently. The PR description says:

> Specifically, the component renderer adds an `inline` key to the render options. In Rails 7.2, the layout was added before this step, so the presence of the inline key didn't affect the layout being applied. In Rails 8, the pipeline was altered so that the component renderer adds the inline key before the layout is applied, which prevents the layout from being included by default.

So in Rails 7.2, the layout was determined BEFORE the component renderer added `inline`. But in Rails 8, the layout is determined AFTER `inline` is added. 

This makes sense. In Rails 7, `_normalize_options` (which checks `_include_layout?`) might be called at a different time. Maybe in Rails 7, `_normalize_options` is called before `_render_to_body_with_renderer`, and in Rails 8 it's called after.

Let me check the commit referenced: `42d75ed3a8b96ee4610601ecde7c40e9d65e003f`

I can't access GitHub, but I can reason about what the fix should be. The fix is to ensure that the layout is applied even when `inline` is used. My proposed fix (adding `layout: true` unless explicitly specified) should work for both Rails 7 and Rails 8.

But wait, I should verify that my fix doesn't break Rails 7 behavior. The test passes with my fix, so that's good.

Now let me also think about edge cases:

1. User passes `layout: false` explicitly - should not apply layout. My fix preserves this because we check `unless render_options.key?(:layout)`.

2. User passes `layout: 'custom_layout'` explicitly - should use custom layout. My fix preserves this.

3. Controller has `layout false` - should not apply layout. My fix sets `layout: true`, which calls `_default_layout` with `require_layout: true`. `_default_layout` checks `action_has_layout?` which returns false if controller has `layout false`. So no layout is applied. Good.

4. Controller has `layout 'custom'` - should use custom layout. My fix sets `layout: true`, which calls `_default_layout`, which calls `_layout`, which returns the custom layout. Good.

5. No layout specified anywhere - should use default layout (controller name). My fix sets `layout: true`, which triggers default layout lookup. Good.

Let me also check if there's another approach: maybe we should use `html:` or `body:` instead of `inline:`?

Looking at the `_include_layout?` method:
```ruby
def _include_layout?(options)
  (options.keys & [:body, :plain, :html, :inline, :partial]).empty? || options.key?(:layout)
end
```

All of `:body`, `:plain`, `:html`, `:inline`, `:partial` skip layouts. So using `html:` instead of `inline:` wouldn't help.

But wait, `inline:` renders an ERB template string, while `html:` renders an HTML-safe string directly. Maybe we should use `html:` instead? Let me check the difference:

- `inline:` renders the string as an ERB template (so `<%= %>` would be evaluated)
- `html:` renders the string as HTML directly (no ERB evaluation)

The HTML generated by `react_component` is just HTML, not ERB. So using `html:` might be more appropriate. But it still skips layouts.

Actually, looking at the `_render_in_priorities` method in `ActionController::Rendering`:

```ruby
def _render_in_priorities(options)
  RENDER_FORMATS_IN_PRIORITY.each do |format|
    return options[format] if options.key?(format)
  end
  nil
end
```

Where `RENDER_FORMATS_IN_PRIORITY = [:body, :plain, :html]`. So if `:html` is present, it's used directly as the response body, bypassing template rendering entirely. But `:inline` goes through template rendering...

Actually, I think the key insight from the PR description is about the order of operations. The Rails commit likely moved the layout determination to happen after the renderer runs. So in Rails 8, `_include_layout?` is called on the options that now include `inline`, causing layouts to be skipped.

My fix should address this correctly. Let me re-apply it

Let me summarize what was done:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe issue was that in Rails 8, the layout is no longer applied when using `render :component` with server-side rendering in react-rails.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe component renderer in `lib/react/rails/railtie.rb` generates HTML and then calls `render` again with an `inline:` key:\n\n```ruby\nrender_options = options.merge(inline: html)\nrender(render_options)\n```\n\nIn Rails' `ActionView::Layouts`, the `_include_layout?` method checks if certain keys (including `:inline`) are present in the render options. When `:inline` is present and `:layout` is not explicitly set, the layout is skipped:\n\n```ruby\ndef _include_layout?(options)\n  (options.keys & [:body, :plain, :html, :inline, :partial]).empty? || options.key?(:layout)\nend\n```\n\nIn Rails 7, the layout was determined before the component renderer added the `inline` key. In Rails 8, [a change in the render pipeline](https://github.com/rails/rails/commit/42d75ed3a8b96ee4610601ecde7c40e9d65e003f) altered the order so that the `inline` key is added before the layout check, preventing the layout from being applied.\n\n### Fix\n\nAdded a single line in `lib/react/rails/railtie.rb` that sets `layout: true` when no explicit layout is specified by the user:\n\n```ruby\nrender_options[:layout] = true unless render_options.key?(:layout)\n```\n\nThis ensures:\n- The default layout is applied when no layout is specified\n- User-specified layouts (like `layout: false` or `layout: 'custom'`) are still respected\n- Controller-level `layout false` still works (because `action_has_layout?` is checked deeper in the pipeline)", role='assistant', tool_calls=None, function_call=None, provider_specific_fields={'refusal': None}), provider_specific_fields={'content_filter_results': {}})], usage=Usage(completion_tokens=420, prompt_tokens=87056, total_tokens=87476, completion_tokens_details=None, prompt_tokens_details=None, audio_prompt_tokens=0), service_tier=None, prompt_filter_results=None)
